The default value was selected\n550:   // so as not to interfere with any smaller configured timeouts that may have\n551:   // existed in configurations prior to the introduction of this feature, while\n552:   // introducing robustness to TCP connections that terminate without a FIN.\n553:   //\n554:   // This idle timeout applies to new streams and is overridable by the\n555:   // :ref:`route-level idle_timeout\n556:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_config.route.v3.RouteAction.idle_timeout>`. Even on a stream in\n557:   // which the override applies, prior to receipt of the initial request\n558:   // headers, the :ref:`stream_idle_timeout\n559:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stream_idle_timeout>`\n560:   // applies. Each time an encode/decode event for headers or data is processed\n561:   // for the stream, the timer will be reset. If the timeout fires, the stream\n562:   // is terminated with a 408 Request Timeout error code if no upstream response\n563:   // header has been received, otherwise a stream reset occurs.\n564:   //\n565:   // If the :ref:`overload action <config_overload_manager_overload_actions>` \"envoy.overload_actions.reduce_timeouts\"\n566:   // is configured, this timeout is scaled according to the value for\n567:   // :ref:`HTTP_DOWNSTREAM_STREAM_IDLE <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.overload.v3.ScaleTimersOverloadActionConfig.TimerType.HTTP_DOWNSTREAM_STREAM_IDLE>`.\n568:   //\n569:   // Note that it is possible to idle timeout even if the wire traffic for a stream is non-idle, due\n570:   // to the granularity of events presented to the connection manager. For example, while receiving\n571:   // very large request headers, it may be the case that there is traffic regularly arriving on the\n572:   // wire while the connection manage is only able to observe the end-of-headers event, hence the\n573:   // stream may still idle timeout.\n574:   //\n575:   // A value of 0 will completely disable the connection manager stream idle\n576:   // timeout, although per-route idle timeout overrides will continue to apply.\n577:   //\n578:   // This timeout is also used as the default value for :ref:`stream_flush_timeout\n579:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stream_flush_timeout>`.\n580:   google.protobuf.Duration stream_idle_timeout = 24\n581:       [(udpa.annotations.security).configure_for_untrusted_downstream = true];\n582: \n583:   // The stream flush timeout for connections managed by the connection manager.\n584:   //\n585:   // If not specified, the value of stream_idle_timeout is used. This is for backwards compatibility\n586:   // since this was the original behavior. In essence this timeout is an override for the\n587:   // stream_idle_timeout that applies specifically to the end of stream flush case.\n588:   //\n589:   // This timeout specifies the amount of time that Envoy will wait for the peer to open enough\n590:   // window to write any remaining stream data once the entirety of stream data (local end stream is\n591:   // true) has been buffered pending available window. In other words, this timeout defends against\n592:   // a peer that does not release enough window to completely write the stream, even though all\n593:   // data has been proxied within available flow control windows. If the timeout is hit in this\n594:   // case, the :ref:`tx_flush_timeout <config_http_conn_man_stats_per_codec>` counter will be\n595:   // incremented. Note that :ref:`max_stream_duration\n596:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HttpProtocolOptions.max_stream_duration>` does not apply to\n597:   // this corner case.\n598:   google.protobuf.Duration stream_flush_timeout = 59;\n599: \n600:   // The amount of time that Envoy will wait for the entire request to be received.\n601:   // The timer is activated when the request is initiated, and is disarmed when the last byte of the\n602:   // request is sent upstream (i.e. all decoding filters have processed the request), OR when the\n603:   // response is initiated. If not specified or set to 0, this timeout is disabled.\n604:   google.protobuf.Duration request_timeout = 28\n605:       [(udpa.annotations.security).configure_for_untrusted_downstream = true];\n606: \n607:   // The amount of time that Envoy will wait for the request headers to be received. The timer is\n608:   // activated when the first byte of the headers is received, and is disarmed when the last byte of\n609:   // the headers has been received. If not specified or set to 0, this timeout is disabled.\n610:   google.protobuf.Duration request_headers_timeout = 41 [\n611:     (validate.rules).duration = {gte {}},\n612:     (udpa.annotations.security).configure_for_untrusted_downstream = true\n613:   ];\n614: \n615:   // The time that Envoy will wait between sending an HTTP/2 “shutdown\n616:   // notification” (GOAWAY frame with max stream ID) and a final GOAWAY frame.\n617:   // This is used so that Envoy provides a grace period for new streams that\n618:   // race with the final GOAWAY frame. During this grace period, Envoy will\n619:   // continue to accept new streams. After the grace period, a final GOAWAY\n620:   // frame is sent and Envoy will start refusing new streams. Draining occurs\n621:   // either when a connection hits the idle timeout, when :ref:`max_connection_duration\n622:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HttpProtocolOptions.max_connection_duration>`\n623:   // is reached, or during general server draining. The default grace period is\n624:   // 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if this option is not specified.\n625:   google.protobuf.Duration drain_timeout = 12;\n626: \n627:   // The delayed close timeout is for downstream connections managed by the HTTP connection manager.\n628:   // It is defined as a grace period after connection close processing has been locally initiated\n629:   // during which Envoy will wait for the peer to close (i.e., a TCP FIN/RST is received by Envoy\n630:   // from the downstream connection) prior to Envoy closing the socket associated with that\n631:   // connection.\n632:   //\n633:   // .. note::\n634:   //\n635:   //   This timeout is enforced even when the socket associated with the downstream connection is pending a flush of\n636:   //   the write buffer. However, any progress made writing data to the socket will restart the timer associated with\n637:   //   this timeout. This means that the total grace period for a socket in this state will be\n638:   //   <total_time_waiting_for_write_buffer_flushes>+<delayed_close_timeout>.\n639:   //\n640:   // Delaying Envoy's connection close and giving the peer the opportunity to initiate the close\n641:   // sequence mitigates a race condition that exists when downstream clients do not drain/process\n642:   // data in a connection's receive buffer after a remote close has been detected via a socket\n643:   // ``write()``. This race leads to such clients failing to process the response code sent by Envoy,\n644:   // which could result in erroneous downstream processing.\n645:   //\n646:   // If the timeout triggers, Envoy will close the connection's socket.\n647:   //\n648:   // The default timeout is 1000 ms if this option is not specified.\n649:   //\n650:   // .. note::\n651:   //    To be useful in avoiding the race condition described above, this timeout must be set\n652:   //    to *at least* <max round trip time expected between clients and Envoy>+<100ms to account for\n653:   //    a reasonable \"worst\" case processing time for a full iteration of Envoy's event loop>.\n654:   //\n655:   // .. warning::\n656:   //    A value of ``0`` will completely disable delayed close processing. When disabled, the downstream\n657:   //    connection's socket will be closed immediately after the write flush is completed or will\n658:   //    never close if the write flush does not complete.\n659:   //\n660:   google.protobuf.Duration delayed_close_timeout = 26;\n661: \n662:   // Configuration for :ref:`HTTP access logs <arch_overview_access_logs>`\n663:   // emitted by the If ALPN data is available, it\\n51:     // is preferred, otherwise protocol inference is used. If the timeout fires, the stream\n562:   // is terminated with a 408 Request Timeout error code if no upstream response\n563:   // header has been received, otherwise a stream reset occurs.\n564:   //\n565:   // If the :ref:`overload action <config_overload_manager_overload_actions>` \"envoy.overload_actions.reduce_timeouts\"\n566:   // is configured, this timeout is scaled according to the value for\n567:   // :ref:`HTTP_DOWNSTREAM_STREAM_IDLE <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.overload.v3.ScaleTimersOverloadActionConfig.TimerType.HTTP_DOWNSTREAM_STREAM_IDLE>`.\n568:   //\n569:   // Note that it is possible to idle timeout even if the wire traffic for a stream is non-idle, due\n570:   // to the granularity of events presented to the connection manager. For example, while receiving\n571:   // very large request headers, it may be the case that there is traffic regularly arriving on the\n572:   // wire while the connection manage is only able to observe the end-of-headers event, hence the\n573:   // stream may still idle timeout.\n574:   //\n575:   // A value of 0 will completely disable the connection manager stream idle\n576:   // timeout, although per-route idle timeout overrides will continue to apply.\n577:   //\n578:   // This timeout is also used as the default value for :ref:`stream_flush_timeout\n579:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stream_flush_timeout>`.\n580:   google.protobuf.Duration stream_idle_timeout = 24\n581:       [(udpa.annotations.security).configure_for_untrusted_downstream = true];\n582: \n583:   // The stream flush timeout for connections managed by the connection manager.\n584:   //\n585:   // If not specified, the value of stream_idle_timeout is used.
